These aren’t actually “new”, but rather “new to me”. I’ve mostly been playing with <a href="http://lesscss.org">LESS</a> and <a href="http://gruntjs.com">Grunt</a>. Grunt accomplishes all sorts of things like minification, linting, and compiling LESS files for me. As I’ve been playing with LESS, I’m discovering more and more things I can do with it. The most recent? LOOPS!</p> <h2 id="the-problem">The Problem</h2> <p>While building my <a href="/blog/2014/04/07/a-simple-css-grid/">css grid</a>, I needed to make literally hundreds of classes for cells, each with calculated width values. LESS was great for performing the math part, all though simple math, I’m lazy. So to be able to loop through the classes I wanted and generate the css for me, I really needed a loop.</p> <h2 id="the-solution">The Solution</h2> <p>My exact solution was a little different than this, as I actually used nested loops. But here’s the basic breakdown of a loop with LESS.</p> <p>First, we set the number of iterations through the loop. The loops actually starts at the top and counts backward to zero.</p> <div class="highlight"><pre><code class="language-css" data-lang="css"><span class="k">@iterations</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="nt">10</span><span class="p">;</span></code></pre></div> <p>Then we make our actual loop. Yes, it’s looks just like a class, but it will never appear in our resulting CSS.</p> <div class="highlight"><pre><code class="language-css" data-lang="css"><span class="nc">.loopClass</span><span class="o">(</span><span class="k">@index</span><span class="o">)</span> <span class="nt">when</span> <span class="o">(</span><span class="k">@index</span> <span class="o">&gt;</span> <span class="nt">0</span><span class="o">)</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="o">//</span><span class="nt">Do</span> <span class="nt">stuff</span> <span class="nt">inside</span> <span class="nt">the</span> <span class="nt">loop</span> <span class="o">...</span> <span class="nc">.loopClass</span><span class="o">(</span><span class="k">@index</span> <span class="nt">-</span> <span class="nt">1</span><span class="o">)</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="o">//</span><span class="nt">next</span> <span class="nt">iteration</span> <span class="p">}</span></code></pre></div> <p>In this loop, I want to create classes classes called <code>.col-*</code>, where <code>*</code> in the index. Each class should have a width equal to <code>(index / interations) * 100</code>. So inside the loop (in place of <code>...</code>) I put the following code:</p> <div class="highlight"><pre><code class="language-css" data-lang="css"><span class="nc">.col-</span><span class="o">@</span><span class="p">{</span><span class="n">index</span><span class="p">}</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">width</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="n">percentage</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">@</span><span class="n">index</span><span class="o">/@</span><span class="n">iterations</span><span class="p">);</span> <span class="p">}</span></code></pre></div> <p>Next, outside of the loop I add some code to make sure it stops when the index hits zero…</p> <div class="highlight"><pre><code class="language-css" data-lang="css"><span class="nc">.loopClass</span><span class="o">(</span><span class="nt">0</span><span class="o">);</span></code></pre></div> <p>…and then call the loop for the first time.</p> <div class="highlight"><pre><code class="language-css" data-lang="css"><span class="nc">.loopClass</span><span class="o">(</span><span class="k">@iterations</span><span class="o">)</span><span class="p">;</span></code></pre></div> <p>That’s all there is. The whole LESS code looks like this:</p> <div class="highlight"><pre><code class="language-css" data-lang="css"><span class="k">@iterations</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="nt">10</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="nc">.loopingClass</span> <span class="o">(</span><span class="k">@index</span><span class="o">)</span> <span class="nt">when</span> <span class="o">(</span><span class="k">@index</span> <span class="o">&gt;</span> <span class="nt">0</span><span class="o">)</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="nc">.col-</span><span class="o">@</span><span class="p">{</span><span class="n">index</span><span class="p">}</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">width</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="n">percentage</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">@</span><span class="n">index</span><span class="o">/@</span><span class="n">iterations</span><span class="p">);</span> <span class="p">}</span> <span class="nc">.loopingClass</span><span class="o">(</span><span class="k">@index</span> <span class="nt">-</span> <span class="nt">1</span><span class="o">)</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span> <span class="nc">.loopingClass</span> <span class="o">(</span><span class="nt">0</span><span class="o">)</span> <span class="p">{}</span> <span class="nc">.loopingClass</span> <span class="o">(</span><span class="k">@iterations</span><span class="o">)</span><span class="p">;</span></code></pre></div> <p>This is the resulting CSS:</p> <div class="highlight"><pre><code class="language-css" data-lang="css"><span class="nc">.col-10</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">width</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="m">100%</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span> <span class="nc">.col-9</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">width</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="m">90%</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span> <span class="nc">.col-8</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">width</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="m">80%</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span> <span class="nc">.col-7</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">width</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="m">70%</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span> <span class="nc">.col-6</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">width</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="m">60%</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span> <span class="nc">.col-5</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">width</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="m">50%</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span> <span class="nc">.col-4</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">width</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="m">40%</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span> <span class="nc">.col-3</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">width</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="m">30%</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span> <span class="nc">.col-2</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">width</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="m">20%</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span> <span class="nc">.col-1</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">width</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="m">10%</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span></code></pre></div> <p>So, it’s actually a pretty simple solution I think. Like I said, I actually used nested calls to 2 different loops, I’ll post details on the in the next day or two.</p> Thu, 10 Apr 2014 09:24:54 -0400 http://markrabey.com/blog/2014/04/10/looping-with-less http://markrabey.com/blog/2014/04/10/looping-with-less More Cells! <p>Yesterday I <a href="/blog/2014/04/07/a-simple-css-grid/">posted</a> the first part of my CSS Grid. Taking a look at it this morning, I’ve decided I need to refactor it a little to allow for a few more classes. Other grids often use the class names <code>.row</code> and/or <code>.col-*</code>. As it is now, I am using <code>.container</code> and <code>.cell-*</code>. I’m going to keep <code>.container</code>, but I’m rethinking <code>.cell-*</code> a little. I was using it simply to describe how much of the whole each cell spanned. Essentially the <code>*</code> was the number of total cells in a <code>.container</code> and that should always equal 12. The problem I quickly ran into, was wanting to create a layout that was 2 columns. One column at 1/3 width, and the other at 2/3. A pretty common layout these days.</p> <p>My solution was to rename these classes to describe the width’s more specifically. I’m going to use <code>.cell-*-*</code>. Where the ‘*’s basically represent the fraction of the whole that each cell makes up. For example, my 2 column layout mentioned above would be coded something like this:</p> <div class="highlight"><pre><code class="language-html" data-lang="html"><span class="nt">&lt;div</span> <span class="na">class=</span><span class="s">&quot;container&quot;</span><span class="nt">&gt;</span> <span class="nt">&lt;div</span> <span class="na">class=</span><span class="s">&quot;cell-1-3&quot;</span><span class="nt">&gt;</span> Some Content <span class="nt">&lt;/div&gt;</span> <span class="nt">&lt;div</span> <span class="na">class=</span><span class="s">&quot;cell-2-3&quot;</span><span class="nt">&gt;</span> Some other content <span class="nt">&lt;/div&gt;</span> <span class="nt">&lt;/div&gt;</span></code></pre></div> <p>By creating this simple <a href="http://lesscss.org">LESS</a> function, I quickly generate the additional classes I need:</p> <div class="highlight"><pre><code class="language-css" data-lang="css"><span class="nc">.generate-container-cells</span><span class="o">(</span><span class="k">@count</span><span class="o">)</span> <span class="nt">when</span> <span class="o">(</span><span class="k">@count</span> <span class="o">&gt;</span> <span class="nt">0</span><span class="o">)</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="nc">.generate-cells</span><span class="o">(</span><span class="k">@count</span><span class="o">)</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="nc">.generate-container-cells</span><span class="o">(</span><span class="k">@count</span> <span class="nt">-</span> <span class="nt">1</span><span class="o">)</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span> <span class="nc">.generate-cells</span><span class="o">(</span><span class="k">@d</span><span class="o">,</span><span class="k">@n</span><span class="nd">:1</span><span class="o">)</span> <span class="nt">when</span> <span class="o">(</span><span class="k">@n</span> <span class="o">&lt;=</span> <span class="k">@d</span><span class="o">)</span><span class="p">{</span> <span class="nc">.cell-</span><span class="o">@</span><span class="p">{</span><span class="n">n</span><span class="p">}</span><span class="nt">-</span><span class="o">@</span><span class="p">{</span><span class="n">d</span><span class="p">}</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">width</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="n">percentage</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">@</span><span class="n">n</span> <span class="o">/</span> <span class="o">@</span><span class="n">d</span><span class="p">);</span> <span class="p">}</span> <span class="nc">.generate-cells</span><span class="o">(</span><span class="k">@d</span><span class="o">,(</span><span class="k">@n</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="nt">1</span><span class="o">))</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="err">}</span></code></pre></div> <p>Again, this isn’t a LESS tutorial so, I won’t go into detail about what this is doing, I’ll save that for another post. The resulting CSS however, looks kind of like this:</p> <div class="highlight"><pre><code class="language-css" data-lang="css"><span class="nc">.cell-1-12</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">width</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="m">8.33333333%</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span> <span class="nc">.cell-2-12</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">width</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="m">16.66666667%</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span> <span class="o">...</span> <span class="nc">.cell-12-12</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">width</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="m">100%</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span> <span class="nc">.cell-1-11</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">width</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="m">9.09090909%</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span> <span class="nc">.cell-2-11</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">width</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="m">18.18181818%</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span> <span class="o">...</span> <span class="nc">.cell-1-1</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">width</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="m">100%</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span></code></pre></div> <p>I didn’t bother putting in everything, it’s long, and true, maybe not the prettiest CSS. But, I am using LESS, so I never really have to look at it. That’s the beautiful thing, the LESS code is about 40 lines, and my generated CSS is about 250. Then, the CSS is minified, which removes some of the messy CSS entirely. Even before minifying, the CSS is only 3kb (2kb after). So, pretty clean if you ask me!</p> <p>I haven’t updated the demo page fully, but you can see here there are no a lot layout more possibilities: <a href="/content/images/blog/2014/Apr/Screen_Shot_2014_04_08_at_5_31_28_AM.png"><img src="/content/images/blog/2014/Apr/Screen_Shot_2014_04_08_at_5_31_28_AM.png" alt="Grid Demo" /></a></p> <p>With this now working more or less the way I want it to, I can move on to making it responsive.</p> <p>I have updated the code on <a href="https://github.com/MarkRabey/markr-grid">GitHub</a> to reflect these changes.</p> Tue, 08 Apr 2014 05:54:48 -0400 http://markrabey.com/blog/2014/04/08/more-cells http://markrabey.com/blog/2014/04/08/more-cells Making the Grid Responsive <p>Every website should be responsive. More and more users are visting sites on their mobile devices, so we need to give them the best possible experience. I hate nothing more than going to a site on my phone and being sent to some ‘m.’ subdomain, or something like that. I can’t help but wonder what I’m missing. If there is something that can be removed from your desktop site, and still give the mobile user the same experience, then that content possibly isn’t needed on your site at all. If you’re willing to offer your users a sub-par experience on mobile, you might want to reconsider what you’re doing altogether. In the majority of cases, you are not building a mobile website, or a desktop website. Rather, you are simply building a website.</p> <h2 id="where-were-we">Where were we?</h2> <p>In a <a href="http://markrabey.com/blog/2014/04/07/a-simple-css-grid/">previous post</a>, I began building a CSS grid system. I left off with the basic foundation of the grid, but still needed to make it responsive. I thought about writing a “mobile first” grid, but I’m working on a desktop, so it seems more suitable to start with that and work down.</p> <h2 id="quick-update">Quick Update</h2> <p>In that it has been quite awile since starting the grid, I have actually reworked it quite a bit. Almost entirely rewritten it, in fact. First, I set a couple of variables. As before I have one variable the maximum number of cells per ‘row’. Next, I have a variable for the ‘gutter’, or space between cells, and finally variables for my responsive breakpoints. My variables look like this:</p> <div class="highlight"><pre><code class="language-css" data-lang="css"><span class="k">@cell-count</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="nt">12</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="k">@grid-gutter</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="nt">1em</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="k">@grid-breakpoint-medium</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="nt">600px</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="k">@grid-breakpoint-large</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="nt">960px</span><span class="p">;</span></code></pre></div> <p>Also, I no longer contain <code>.cell-*</code> in a <code>.container</code>, but rather the ‘container’ gets a class called <code>.grid</code>.</p> <h2 id="responsive">Responsive</h2> <p>I decided that in order to make the grid responsive, I would add different classes to cells that would be affected at different breakpoints. First, I had to adjust the <a href="/blog/2014/04/10/looping-with-less/">mixins I used as loops</a> to create the cells. I added a prefix argument that gets passed into the loop. So now, my main cells are generated like so:</p> <div class="highlight"><pre><code class="language-css" data-lang="css"><span class="nt">gridLoop</span><span class="o">(</span><span class="k">@count</span><span class="o">,</span><span class="k">@cell-prefix</span><span class="o">)</span> <span class="nt">when</span> <span class="o">(</span><span class="k">@count</span> <span class="o">&gt;</span> <span class="nt">0</span><span class="o">)</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="nc">.cellLoop</span><span class="o">(</span><span class="k">@d</span><span class="o">:</span><span class="k">@count</span><span class="o">,</span><span class="k">@cell-prefix</span><span class="o">:</span><span class="k">@cell-prefix</span><span class="o">)</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="nc">.gridLoop</span><span class="o">(</span><span class="k">@count</span> <span class="nt">-</span> <span class="nt">1</span><span class="o">,</span><span class="k">@cell-prefix</span><span class="o">)</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="err">}</span> <span class="nc">.cellLoop</span><span class="o">(</span><span class="k">@d</span><span class="o">,</span><span class="k">@n</span><span class="nd">:1</span><span class="o">,</span><span class="k">@cell-prefix</span><span class="o">)</span> <span class="nt">when</span> <span class="o">(</span><span class="k">@n</span> <span class="o">&lt;</span> <span class="k">@d</span><span class="o">)</span><span class="p">{</span> <span class="o">.@</span><span class="p">{</span><span class="n">cell</span><span class="o">-</span><span class="n">prefix</span><span class="p">}</span><span class="nt">-</span><span class="o">@</span><span class="p">{</span><span class="n">n</span><span class="p">}</span><span class="nt">-</span><span class="o">@</span><span class="p">{</span><span class="n">d</span><span class="p">}</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">width</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="n">percentage</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">@</span><span class="n">n</span> <span class="o">/</span> <span class="o">@</span><span class="n">d</span><span class="p">);</span> <span class="p">}</span> <span class="nc">.cellLoop</span><span class="o">(</span><span class="k">@d</span><span class="o">,(</span><span class="k">@n</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="nt">1</span><span class="o">),</span><span class="k">@cell-prefix</span><span class="o">)</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="err">}</span> <span class="nc">.gridLoop</span><span class="o">(</span><span class="k">@cell-count</span><span class="o">,</span><span class="nt">cell</span><span class="o">)</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="nc">.cell-1-1</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="nt">width</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="nt">100</span><span class="o">%;</span> <span class="p">}</span></code></pre></div> <p>The last 2 lines here are really what result in code being produced. Calling <code>.gridLoop(@cell-count,cell)</code> generates cells beginning with <code>cell-</code>. Adding <code>.cell-1-1</code> is done because my ‘loop’ does generate <code>.@{cell-prefix}-1-1</code>. Then for my breakpoints I simple have this:</p> <div class="highlight"><pre><code class="language-css" data-lang="css"><span class="k">@media</span> <span class="nt">only</span> <span class="nt">screen</span> <span class="nt">and</span> <span class="o">(</span><span class="nt">min-width</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="k">@grid-breakpoint-medium</span><span class="o">)</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="nc">.gridLoop</span><span class="o">(</span><span class="k">@cell-count</span><span class="o">,</span><span class="nt">medium-cell</span><span class="o">)</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="nc">.medium-cell-1-1</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">width</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="m">100%</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span> <span class="p">}</span> <span class="k">@media</span> <span class="nt">only</span> <span class="nt">screen</span> <span class="nt">and</span> <span class="o">(</span><span class="nt">min-width</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="k">@grid-breakpoint-large</span><span class="o">)</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="nc">.gridLoop</span><span class="o">(</span><span class="k">@cell-count</span><span class="o">,</span><span class="nt">large-cell</span><span class="o">)</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="nc">.large-cell-1-1</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">width</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="m">100%</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span> <span class="p">}</span></code></pre></div> <p>These call the same mixins, but pass in different prefixes. Now, in I add different classes to my HTML for different screen sizes. For example, I have this HTML:</p> <div class="highlight"><pre><code class="language-html" data-lang="html"><span class="nt">&lt;div</span> <span class="na">class=</span><span class="s">&quot;grid&quot;</span><span class="nt">&gt;</span> <span class="nt">&lt;div</span> <span class="na">class=</span><span class="s">&quot;cell-1-1&quot;</span><span class="nt">&gt;</span> <span class="nt">&lt;h1&gt;</span>Grid Demo<span class="nt">&lt;/h1&gt;</span> <span class="nt">&lt;/div&gt;</span> <span class="nt">&lt;/div&gt;</span> <span class="nt">&lt;div</span> <span class="na">class=</span><span class="s">&quot;grid&quot;</span><span class="nt">&gt;</span> <span class="nt">&lt;div</span> <span class="na">class=</span><span class="s">&quot;cell-1-1 medium-cell-1-2 large-cell-1-3&quot;</span><span class="nt">&gt;</span> <span class="nt">&lt;div</span> <span class="na">class=</span><span class="s">&quot;box-content&quot;</span><span class="nt">&gt;</span>.cell-1-1 .medium-cell-1-2 .large-cell-1-3<span class="nt">&lt;/div&gt;</span> <span class="nt">&lt;/div&gt;</span> <span class="nt">&lt;div</span> <span class="na">class=</span><span class="s">&quot;cell-1-1 medium-cell-1-2 large-cell-1-3&quot;</span><span class="nt">&gt;</span> <span class="nt">&lt;div</span> <span class="na">class=</span><span class="s">&quot;box-content&quot;</span><span class="nt">&gt;</span>.cell-1-1 .medium-cell-1-2 .large-cell-1-3<span class="nt">&lt;/div&gt;</span> <span class="nt">&lt;/div&gt;</span> <span class="nt">&lt;div</span> <span class="na">class=</span><span class="s">&quot;cell-1-1 medium-cell-1-1 large-cell-1-3&quot;</span><span class="nt">&gt;</span> <span class="nt">&lt;div</span> <span class="na">class=</span><span class="s">&quot;box-content&quot;</span><span class="nt">&gt;</span>.cell-1-1 .medium-cell-1-1 .large-cell-1-3<span class="nt">&lt;/div&gt;</span> <span class="nt">&lt;/div&gt;</span> <span class="nt">&lt;/div&gt;</span></code></pre></div> <p>Which produces this result when the window is greater than 960px wide: <img src="/content/images/blog/2014/May/Screen-Shot-2014-05-26-at-2-32-15-PM.png" alt="960px" /></p> <p>And then at less than 960px, but greater than 600px: <img src="/content/images/blog/2014/May/Screen-Shot-2014-05-26-at-2-33-55-PM.png" alt="600-900" /></p> <p>And finally, less than 600px: <img src="/content/images/blog/2014/May/Screen-Shot-2014-05-26-at-2-34-37-PM.png" alt="less than 600px" /></p> <p>There is still a slight issue I want to work on with that right margin, but that’s on the way. Likely not in blog form.</p> <p>This update should be on <a href="https://github.com/MarkRabey/markr-grid&quot;target=&quot;_blank">GitHub</a> very soon, I just need to rewrite the readme file.</p> Mon, 07 Apr 2014 13:19:46 -0400 http://markrabey.com/blog/2014/04/07/making-the-grid-responsive http://markrabey.com/blog/2014/04/07/making-the-grid-responsive css, grid, layout, less A Simple CSS Grid <h2 id="really">Really?!</h2> <p>I’m working on templates and things for samples, as well as working on my own theme for this blog. I like grids, so I’m making one.</p> <p>I know, the world doesn’t really need <em>another</em> css grid, but hear me out!</p> <p>I really wanted to make my own grid system for 2 reasons:</p> <ol> <li>To learn how these things work. Simple, I know, but I like to know exactly what I’m working with</li> <li>I’ve worked with <a href="http://getbootstrap.com">Bootstrap</a>, and like it, but as I’m trying to become a better front-end engineer, I don’t want to use anything for a grid that also styles elements for me. I know everything in Bootstrap can be overwritten, but I’m tired of doing that. I want to build from the ground up.</li> </ol> <p>I should note, that I’m trying to ignore grids I’ve already worked with. One thing I really hate about most grid systems in the class names. I don’t find <code>.row</code> or <code>.col-*</code> particularily useful. Mostly because when designing for mobile these class names are inaccurate. On a mobile device, a <code>div</code> with <code>.row</code> really looks like a column, and <code>.col-*</code> is really just a cell in that column. So, instead of <code>.col-*</code>, I am choosing to use <code>.cell-*</code>. That seems more accurate. The “row” is really just a container for the cells, so I’m calling it…<code>.container</code>. I’m writing everything using <a href="http://lesscss.org/">LESS</a>. I find it makes things nice and clean, and it will do a lot of the math for me.</p> <p>It’s also important to note that I am writing the code as I write this post, so I haven’t tested anything. At the end I will test and post the final CSS.</p> <h2 id="getting-started">Getting Started</h2> <p>To get going, I needed to decide the maximum number of cells per row. My first thought was to try to allow an infinte number. I quickly decided that was both difficult, and impractical. Then, trying to be “better” than the Bootstrap, I decided as long as it was more than 12, I was good. You can actually get custom Bootstrap builds with as many or few <code>.grid-columns</code> as you would like. So, picking a number out of spite wasn’t an option.</p> <p>Odd numbers were out. I wanted something that could easily divide into 2 even columns. That just seemed obvious. I thought about 10, but many common layouts use 3 columns, or at least 1/3 and 2/3 column layout. So, an even number, divisable by 3. I considered 6, but that just doesn’t seem like enough. I also remembered a layout I did once that was 4 even columns, so 6 didn’t really work. I decided I actually liked 12 best. I could have gone to 18 or 24, but that just seemed excessive. I think I understand now why most of these other grids default to 12.</p> <p>To keep my cell names simple, I decided the <code>*</code> in <code>.cell-*</code> would be a number representing the total number in that <code>.container</code>.</p> <p>All cells need to float so they line up all pretty-like, I want to minimize the amount of code I actually write, and I want to add some padding to each cell. Here is what my LESS looks like:</p> <div class="highlight"><pre><code class="language-css" data-lang="css"><span class="k">@cell-padding</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="nt">10px</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="o">[</span><span class="nt">class</span><span class="o">^=</span><span class="s1">&#39;cell-&#39;</span><span class="o">]</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">float</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="k">left</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="k">padding</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="o">@</span><span class="n">cell</span><span class="o">-</span><span class="k">padding</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span> <span class="o">[</span><span class="nt">class</span><span class="o">^=</span><span class="s1">&#39;cell-&#39;</span><span class="o">]</span><span class="nd">:last-of-type</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">float</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="k">right</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="k">padding-right</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="o">@</span><span class="n">cell</span><span class="o">-</span><span class="k">padding</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span> <span class="nc">.container</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">clear</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="k">both</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span></code></pre></div> <p>I set the padding as a variable, because I honestly don’t know exactly what that will be when I’m done. LESS allows me to change it in that one spot, and affect the entire CSS. Here is the resulting CSS:</p> <div class="highlight"><pre><code class="language-css" data-lang="css"><span class="o">[</span><span class="nt">class</span><span class="o">^=</span><span class="s1">&#39;cell-&#39;</span><span class="o">]</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">float</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="k">left</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="k">padding</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="m">10px</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span> <span class="o">[</span><span class="nt">class</span><span class="o">^=</span><span class="s1">&#39;cell-&#39;</span><span class="o">]</span><span class="nd">:last-of-type</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">float</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="k">right</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="k">padding-right</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="m">10px</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span> <span class="nc">.container</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">clear</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="k">both</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span></code></pre></div> <p>The selector <code>[class^='cell-']</code> targets any element with a class beginning with “cell-“. This selector will save me lots of time! Floating the last <code>.cell-*</code> in a <code>.container</code> to the right, corrects any padding to width issues I might have. I then clear the floats on the <code>.container</code> elements, so that each one creates a new “row”.</p> <p>Figuring out the widths for each possible <code>.cell-*</code> is actually really simple math. In that each cell is a fraction of a whole, I can just divide by 12. For example, 100 ÷ 5 = 20, so the width of <code>.cell-5</code> would be 20%. It’s even easier if I let LESS do the work! I actally added a variable to the top of my LESS file to hold the number of cells in a container, just in case I change my mind later.</p> <div class="highlight"><pre><code class="language-css" data-lang="css"><span class="k">@container-cells</span><span class="nd">:12</span><span class="p">;</span></code></pre></div> <p>Looping through the values 1-12 with less was pretty simple, but this is not a LESS tutorial in any regard, so I will only post the resulting CSS.</p> <div class="highlight"><pre><code class="language-css" data-lang="css"><span class="nc">.cell-12</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">width</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="m">8.33333333%</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span> <span class="nc">.cell-11</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">width</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="m">9.09090909%</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span> <span class="nc">.cell-10</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">width</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="m">10%</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span> <span class="nc">.cell-9</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">width</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="m">11.11111111%</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span> <span class="nc">.cell-8</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">width</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="m">12.5%</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span> <span class="nc">.cell-7</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">width</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="m">14.28571429%</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span> <span class="nc">.cell-6</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">width</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="m">16.66666667%</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span> <span class="nc">.cell-5</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">width</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="m">20%</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span> <span class="nc">.cell-4</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">width</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="m">25%</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span> <span class="nc">.cell-3</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">width</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="m">33.33333333%</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span> <span class="nc">.cell-2</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">width</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="m">50%</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span> <span class="nc">.cell-1</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">width</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="m">100%</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span></code></pre></div> <p>While building an example page, I found some padding issues. I corrected it simply by adding this to the top my css:</p> <div class="highlight"><pre><code class="language-css" data-lang="css"><span class="o">*,</span> <span class="o">*</span><span class="nd">:after</span><span class="o">,</span> <span class="o">*</span><span class="nd">:before</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">margin</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="m">0</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="k">padding</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="m">0</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="c">/* Removes padding behaviour on widths */</span> <span class="o">-</span><span class="n">webkit</span><span class="o">-</span><span class="n">box</span><span class="o">-</span><span class="n">sizing</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="k">border</span><span class="o">-</span><span class="n">box</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="o">-</span><span class="n">moz</span><span class="o">-</span><span class="n">box</span><span class="o">-</span><span class="n">sizing</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="k">border</span><span class="o">-</span><span class="n">box</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="n">box</span><span class="o">-</span><span class="n">sizing</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="k">border</span><span class="o">-</span><span class="n">box</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span></code></pre></div> <p>The results is something like this: <img src="/content/images/blog/2014/Apr/Screen_Shot_2014_04_07_at_12_52_33_PM.png" alt="" /></p> <p>As you can see, it’s pretty simple. But there is something major left to do: <em>make it responsive!</em></p> <p>That will be the next post. Coming soon!</p> <p>You can track the project on <a href="https://github.com/MarkRabey/markr-grid">GitHub</a>.</p> Mon, 07 Apr 2014 11:38:02 -0400 http://markrabey.com/blog/2014/04/07/a-simple-css-grid http://markrabey.com/blog/2014/04/07/a-simple-css-grid css, grid, layout, less It's only temporary. <p>You guessed right. On my blog I am currently using a theme designed by someone else. I’m sure you’re wondering why I’m using a theme, when I am, in fact, a web designer. There are two important things to keep in mind regarding this:</p> <ol> <li>I at least chose a nice theme.</li> <li>It’s only temporary.</li> </ol> <p>I am currently working on developing themes for the <a href="http://ghost.org">Ghost</a> blogging platform. It’s my latest love. I’ve only been using it for a day or 2 now, and I’m hooked.</p> <h2 id="why-ghost">Why Ghost?</h2> <p>I discovered it while doing some reading on <a href="http://nodejs.org">Node.js</a>. I was considering building myself a new blogging platform using Node. I’ve done something like that before. I wanted to get comfortable using ColdFusion and Object-Relational Mapping (ORM). So I built myself a simple blog using it. Some people build “Hello World”, I make a blog.</p> <p>The more I think about this though, the more I hate myself for doing it. I tend to get as far as a “proof of concept” then stop. Often, I stop blogging altogether for several months or years after the blog is built. It’s also pretty impractical. I mean, my end goal is pretty much always the same: “Make it do what Wordpress does, but better, because Wordpress sucks”.</p> <p>After that last ColdFusion blog, I was left wondering why I thought Wordpress sucked. It didn’t. There are litterally hundreds of thousands of themes and plugins to do all sorts of stuff! So, why not just use it? It works, right? Yes. It works. It even works really well in some cases. So, I decided to give Wordpress another shot. I moved everything over to <a href="http://wideasleepdad.com">a new blog</a>. YAY! Ok, so I load up, it installs nice, I blog a bit for <em>maybe</em> a month. Then I remembered that I’m a <strong><em>Web Guy</em></strong>. I build things for the <strong><em>web</em></strong>. I decided I needed to start building Wordpress themes. What better way to express my creativity, and show off skill than to make money developing Wordpress themes? How hard can it be?</p> <p>Well…<strong><em>IT’S REALLY HARD</em></strong>. Not really I suppose, but my point is that it’s <em>much</em> harder than it needs to be. The Wordpress API is terrible. Probably because Wordpress is written in PHP, and I <em>hate</em> PHP. I’m honestly not sure why I hate PHP, I’ve just found that there are far better languages out there, and PHP is only used because it’s free, and it’s not ASP.</p> <p>Over the past year, I’ve been experimenting with Node.js, and the idea of serverside JavaScript. I love it. So, when I decided to to dive in deeper, the natural platform was Node, and I didn’t want to build my own again. I came across Ghost and quickly discovered how simple it is to design and build for. It has just enough in it for what I want. I quickly fell in love. I don’t know why I’m so in love. It’s just a blogging platform.</p> <h2 id="now-what">Now what?</h2> <p>Now I want to work on becoming a better front-end developer. I really believe that we as designers need to do better for our users. We need a user’s experience on the web to be positive in every regard. If it’s something we have control over, we need to do everything in our power to pass that control and that power to the end user.</p> <p>I’m going to start with trying to get some of my little projects polished off and onto GitHub, then start working on my <em>own</em> theme for my blog, then start making themes for others.
